3GPP TSG RAN WG1 #125 R1-260xxxx

Dalian, May 18th ~ 22nd, 2026

Agenda item: 10.8.3

Source: Moderator (LG Electronics)

Title: Summary on Waveform and frame structure for 6G ISAC

Document for: Discussion/Decision

Introduction

In RAN #108, the SID on Study on 6G Radio was agreed, which includes the following objectives for 6G ISAC [1].

[TABLE]
Sensing – Studies to be based on use cases and associated requirements, as defined in [TR38.914] PHY functions and procedures for sensing technology (e.g., waveform. reference signals, measurement feedback, etc…) [RAN1, RAN4] Evaluate sensing performance and if necessary, extend channel modelling, for the selected use cases [RAN1] Aspects of integration with communication services [RAN1] higher layer procedures and protocol aspects [RAN2] RAN4 aspects of sensing including RF, coexistence, and testability in coordination with other WGs [RAN4] Note: RAN1 identify detailed requirements, if triggered by TSG RAN

This document summarizes the contributions and discussions on sub-agenda 10.8.3 Waveform and frame structure for ISAC.

[TABLE]
ISAC Note 1: Including PHY functionalities and procedures for ISAC Evaluations Note 1: Including deployment scenarios, performance evaluation methodologies/metrics/KPIs for the target use cases, and potential extension of channel model, if necessary, Aspects of integration with communication Note 1: Including proposals for reusing and dedicated reference signal based on waveforms for communications, measurement and report for different use cases, etc. (could be part of AI 10.5.3) Waveform and frame structure Note 1: Including proposals for potential enhancement based on communication waveform (e.g., low PAPR waveform enhancement, longer CP length, larger SCS etc.), potential new waveform, frame structure, and corresponding analysis on performance benefit and impact in terms of integration with communication.

This document follows the convention below for improving readability:

The proposals in this document are tagged with different color based on discussion priority:

[H] Proposal: Proposal to be discussed with High Priority.

[M] Proposal: Proposal to be discussed with Medium Priority.

[L] Proposal: Proposal to be discussed with Low Priority

The proposal version (the last digit of the proposal number) will increase if there is any update on the proposal from the previous round. If there is no update on the proposal from the previous round, there will be no increase on the proposal version.

This agenda will cover the following topics:

Waveform

CP-OFDM enhancement for 6G ISAC

Sensing RS sequence design

Other waveforms for 6G ISAC

Frame structure

CP enhancement for 6G ISAC

SCS enhancement for 6G ISAC

Evaluation of waveform/frame structure

Evaluation based on waveform characteristics analysis

Evaluation based on Link-Level Simulation

The following topics will be covered by agenda 10.8.2

Resource allocation & Multiplexing of sensing signal

Sensing RS pattern design

The following topics will be covered by agenda 10.8.1

LLS channel modeling for 6G ISAC

For more constructive discussions within very limited time schedule for 6G SI ISAC agenda, Moderator tried to make FL Proposals based on the contributions supported by majority of companies, rather than a single or a few companies.

Proposed online/offline proposals

Monday

Tuesday

[H] Proposal 4.1.1-4

At least the following enhancement directions for CP-OFDM are studied for 6G ISAC.

Enhancement to PAPR/Output Back-Off(OBO)/Tx power gain

Enhancement to [Ambiguity Function(AF)]/auto-correlation properties (PSLR/ISLR, main lobe width)

Enhancement to joint PAPR and AF properties

Resilience to interference

[Resilience to ACLR(Adjacent Channel Leakage Ratio)/OOBE(Out-Of-Band Emission)]

Enhancement to improve sensing resource utilization efficiency

Enhancement to sensing coverage

Enhancement to cross-correlation

Other enhancements are not precluded.

Any combination of multiple enhancements are not precluded.

[FL2][H] Proposal 5.1.1-2

CP length extension by numerology and the impact on the number of symbols per slot

Effective CP length extension based on frequency-domain comb pattern

Time gap before/after/within sensing signal

Effective CP length extension based on phase continuity across successive symbols

Transmission of RS in successive N OFDM symbols without CP length extension

RS sequence enhancement across symbols

By implementation withtout any spec impact

FFS: applicable sensing modes

FFS: whether applicable to dedicated sensing RS or RS shared with communication

FFS: impact on integration with communication

Other methods are not precluded.

Note: RAN1 strives for a solution that has maximum commonality with 6GR communication frame structure and numerology.

Friday

Proposed offline proposals

Waveform discussions

CP-OFDM enhancements

Background:

There are contributions on the enhancement for sensing to 6GR CP-OFDM based on the relevant necessity and benefits on the following aspects.

PAPR – Nokia, Lekha Wireless, CATT, CICTCI, Xiaomi, Interdigital, China Telcom, NIST, ZTE, Quectel, Shanghai Jiao Tong University, NERCDTV, Offino, China Unicom, LGE

Ambiguity function – Nokia, CATT, CICTCI, Interdigital, Huawei, HiSilicon, China Telcom, NIST, China Unicom

PSLR/ISLR – Nokia, Sharp, CATT, CICTCI, Huawei, HiSilicon, NIST, ZTE

Main lobe width - CATT, CICTCI

ACLR/OOBE – Interdigital, China Telcom

Cross-correlation - CATT, CICTCI, vivo, Interdigital

Weak target detection - Xiaomi

OFDM-based LFM/FMCW-type waveform – Nokia, Interdigital, Samsung, ZTE, ETRI, DOCOMO, LGE

OFDM-based pulse-type waveform – Xiaomi, CMCC, OPPO, Samsung, Lenovo, ZTE, Shanghai Jiao Tong University, NERCDTV, Qualcomm, DOCOMO, LGE, Interdigital, Lenovo, Interdigital, Google

Phase continuity across symbols – vivo (phase compensation for guard band subcarriers)

Phase coded OFDM - Lekha Wireless

Pulse shaping – Sharp, Southeast University

Zak-OTFS-over-CP-OFDM – Cohere Tech

Time-domain and/or frequency-domain processing of sensing signals - Interdigital

Resilience to ISI/ICI – Interdigital, PCL

Full duplex operation - Interdigital

Tx power gain – Huawei, HiSilicon

Self-interference mitigation – NIST

Controlled spectrum spreading/spectrum extension – Quectel

Range ambiguity - Shanghai Jiao Tong University, NERCDTV

According to the contributions, the benefits of introducing Chirp-type waveform include:

Low PAPR

Good autocorrelation

Low Rx complexity

Robustness to interference

Efficient full duplex operation

The benefits of introducing Pulse-type waveform include:

Large sensing coverage for 6G ISAC

Support full duplex without hardware modification

Overhead reduction for multi-static sensing

Measurement utilization potentially for sensing assisting communication

Equivalent to a long CP/GP length

Based on the above observations, Following FL proposal was made for further discussions.

[H] Proposal 4.1.1-3

Agreement: At least the following potential enhancement directions for CP-OFDM are studied for 6G ISAC.

Improve PAPR

Obtain Tx power gain from other

Improve Ambiguity Function (AF)/Auto-correlation properties (PSLR/ISLR, main lobe width)

FFS: details of the definitions, time/frequency/doppler domain, linear correlation vs circular correlation, etc.

Improve resilience to interference

Improve sensing resource utilization efficiency

Improve cross-correlation property

FFS: details of the definition

Note: Other enhancements and any combination of multiple enhancements are not precluded.

At least the following aspects are considered for above potential enhancement directions for CP-OFDM for 6G ISAC.

Impact to ACLR(Adjacent Channel Leakage Ratio)/OOBE(Out-Of-Band Emission)

Impact to ISI/ICI/self-interference/inter-cell interference

Impact to Tx/Rx complexity

Impact to communication (e.g., resource, interference)

Impact from one enhancement to other enhancements

Tiami | Yes but | In our draft, we provided Proposal 7 in R1-2604571: In case Enhanced CP-OFDM is considered for 6GR sensing, RAN1 should prioritize the waveform characteristics’ assessment first to ensure the coexistence with 6GR CP-OFDM communication waveform, such as: Peak-to-Average Power ratio (PAPR). OOBE/ACLR for coexistence with 6GR communications waveform considering non-linear PA model. Ambiguity function (assess the Peak-to-Sidelobe ratio (PSLR)). ZTE | Generally Yes | Generally agree with this proposal, and we have some suggestions. For pulse and FMCW, we see many companies’ interests, but we also see some concerns of viewing pulse/LFM as a new waveform. Therefore, we prefer to study pulse/LFM RS instead of pulse/LFM waveform. Also, we should have a comprehensive study to make sure we don’t miss any chances to improve the ISAC performance, and we also see something in the previous proposal is missed. Based on the above, we have the following suggestions: At least the following CP-OFDM enhancements are studied for 6G ISAC. CATT, CICTCI | Yes | Regarding sensing waveform design, we suggest the following key principles: PAPR and AF properties must be the primary metrics for any CP-OFDM enhancement. For emulating LFM via CP-OFDM, we should prioritize compatibility with NR frequency-domain mapping and reuse legacy sequences like ZC to simplify implementation.
vivo | No | In our contribution, guard band reuse with symbol-phase continuity is a waveform enhancement and should be included. Although only vivo propose this enhanced waveform, according to our reviewing, there is no company to have objection for its inclusion as the waveform enhancement with technical reasons. This means that the supportive ratio is 100%. Therefore, our suggestion is to add a bullet as Enhancement to guard band reuse with symbol-phase continuity. Regarding AF, we need to have a clear definition, that should be aligned with OFDM processing by using circular auto-correlation (or circular matched filter). It should be noted that if defining a circular auto-correlation for AF, AF becomes a 2D-DFT. It can be very easy to prove it by substituting the sampled time domain OFDM signal into AF. For the details, you can refer to Proposal 7.1 where we provide the derivations. Therefore, we suggest removing it until we define AF. According to our analysis, CP-OFDM-based LFM/FMCW/Chirp-type waveform is the same as ZC with the root q=1, it is not related to the waveform other than sequence design. In case of ZC root . Therefore, we suggest removing it as an enhancement of waveform. The final proposal should be as: At least the following CP-OFDM enhancements are studied for 6G ISAC. Enhancement to PAPR/Output Back-Off(OBO)/Tx power gain/Net gain Enhancement to guard band reuse with symbol-phase continuity. Enhancement to Ambiguity Function(AF) properties Enhancement to generate CP-OFDM-based pulse-type waveform Enhancement to generate CP-OFDM-based LFM/FMCW/Chirp-type waveform Enhancement to time-domain cross-correlation/ambiguity Other enhancements are not precluded. To align guard band reuse with other waveform factors, a new proposal is necessary as follows: [H] Proposal 4.3.5 Use of 6GR guard band for sensing is studied for 6G ISAC. It is encouraged that companies provide the technical reasons for supporting/not-supporting.

We can support: Enhancement to PAPR/Output Back-Off(OBO)/Tx power gain/Net gain Enhancement to Ambiguity Function(AF) properties Enhancement to time-domain cross-correlation/ambiguity These 2 items below need to be revised: Enhancement to generate CP-OFDM-based pulse-type waveform Enhancement to generate CP-OFDM-based LFM/FMCW/Chirp-type waveform There is also a related discussion in Proposal 5.1.1, should we also capture here? CEWiT | Yes | We agree with the proposal as it covers all the aspects of enhancements of CP-OFDM waveform
Huawei, HiSilicon | Yes, but | We understand that the purpose of the proposal is to identify the research directions which reaches a certain level of consensus, such as low-PAPR. However, the following two items appear to be more related to specific waveform-generation solutions rather than research directions: Enhancement to generate CP-OFDM-based pulse-type waveform Enhancement to generate CP-OFDM-based LFM/FMCW/Chirp-type waveform In our view, the main benefit of generating CP-OFDM-based pulse-type or CP-OFDM-based LFM/FMCW/Chirp-type waveforms is primarily obtained in the monostatic sensing case. On top of that, some companies also discussed the possibility that UEs may receive such signals in bistatic sensing in order to reduce overhead, while the same signal is used for monostatic sensing. Therefore, we suggest that this research direction be captured in a more general manner, which is overhead reduction for both monostatic and bistatic sensing, rather than specifying particular waveform-generation solutions, and other solutions can list as sub-bullet below. For example, the item could be reformulated as follows: At least the following CP-OFDM enhancements are studied for 6G ISAC. Enhancement to PAPR/Output Back-Off(OBO)/Tx power gain/Net gain Enhancement to Ambiguity Function (AF) properties Enhancement to reduce overhead for monostatic and bistatic sensing, including potential waveform designs based on CP-OFDM Enhancement to time-domain cross-correlation/ambiguity
QC | Yes | Agree in general.
IDCC | Comment | We proposed CP-OFDM-compatible enhancements based on time-domain and/or frequency-domain processing of sensing signals/resources in our TDoc with simulation results. This covers processing applied to sequence generation, resource mapping, OFDM-symbol-level samples, and receiver-side sensing processing. Such processing can improve reflected-signal detectability, delay/Doppler estimation, ambiguity behaviour, and operating SNR region while maintaining compatibility with the baseline CP-OFDM RF chain. E.g., [R1-2604045] Figure 1: Example comparison of baseline CP-OFDM reuse and transform-based enhancement. Since the proposal includes both metric (e.g., PAPR) and generation (e.g., pulse-type), we therefore suggest capturing CP-OFDM enhancement aspect for completeness. Also suggest removing the empty bullet. [H] Proposal 4.1.1 At least the following CP-OFDM enhancements are studied for 6G ISAC. Enhancement to PAPR/Output Back-Off(OBO)/Tx power gain/Net gain Enhancement to Ambiguity Function(AF) properties Enhancement to generate CP-OFDM-based pulse-type waveform Enhancement to time-domain and/or frequency-domain processing of CP-OFDM sensing signals/resources Enhancement to generate CP-OFDM-based LFM/FMCW/Chirp-type waveform Enhancement to time-domain cross-correlation/ambiguity

We suggest adding a specific bullet: "Enhancement to address ISI/ICI in high-Doppler channels, including both mitigation and potential exploitation for sensing".

Samsung |  | We would like to clarify some points. We would like to clarify that all listed enhancements are based on sensing RS design. Separate waveform characteristics (what to enhance) from enhancement approaches (how to enhance). The current list mixes properties such as PAPR and AF with generation directions such as pulse-type or LFM-type, which belong to different dimensions. Classification of enhancement approaches into frequency-domain and time-domain categories is needed. Note: Any CP-OFDM-based enhancement should not increase the receiver processing complexity compared to the basic CP-OFDM reception complexity

Background:

There are number of contributions regarding RS sequence enhancement as follows.

CSI-RS, SRS for type-1/2 resource - Huawei, HiSilicon

Gold sequence – vivo, Huawei, HiSilicon(GS+FDSS), ZTE, DOCOMO (pi/2 BPSK)

ZC sequence – vivo, CATT, CICTCI (Gold sequence w/ QPSK, ZC sequence, Gold sequence with pi/2-BPSK), Huawei/HiSilicon (ZC+FDSS, OQAM(pi/2-BPSK)+FDSS, longer ZC across multiple symbols), ZTE(ZC-based pulse), Shanghai Jiao Tong University, NERCDTV (pulse-type), Qualcom (enhanced ZC for FMCW-like waveform), DOCOMO (root index)

Quasi-complementary sequence set (QCSS) – Huawei, HiSilicon

RS sequence to generate Chirp/LFM/FMCW-type - Apple (OFDM-based ZC for FMCW-like), CATT, CICTCI (compatible to existing RS config.), Interdigital, Samsung (modified ZC)

NLFM(Non-Linear FM) – ZTE, Shanghai Jiao Tong University, NERCDTV

RS sequence to generate pulse-type - Xiaomi

RS sequence randomization in time domain – vivo, Xiaomi

There are contributions about improving PAPR and/or AF properties, contributions about generation of Chirp-type and pulse-type waveform, and contribution about improving the cross-correlation. The following proposals were made based on these observations.

In terms of AF performance enhancement, FDSS is recommended for sidelobe suppression, which can effectively boost sensing capabilities, for instance, lowering false alarm probability (FAP). Ericsson |  | We agree with Huawei’s views that pulse-based solution is a “sensing coverage enhancement” only for aNB monostatic sensing mode. So just by adding an FFS on which mode it is applicable does not include the fundamental assumption about pulse wave for sensing coverage enhancement. TRP-UE bistatic coverage is primarily limited by bistatic geometry, UE receiver capability, synchronization and pathloss of the reflected pathloss. The TRP might transmit into different directions for TRP-UE and TRP-TRP&TRP mono sensing, making reuse impossible or less interesting. Short pulse waveform has very little energy which reduces coverage if self-interference is no issue, so reuse can only happen over a small coverage area of “normal” TRP-UE sensing area.It is also worthy to note that UEs have higher noise figure, smaller antennas, etc., so a reduced power will greatly reduce UE sensing range. UE would need an extra receiver. Different vendors may also use differently long short pulses, since the pulse length determines the blind zone which must be covered by FD-based sensing (which is very much determined by HW capability at BS).

IDCC |  | We support studying CP-OFDM-compatible methods for sensing-resource overhead reduction. However, the proposal should not be limited to a single method, i.e., phase compensation on guard-band sensing resource blocks. Other overhead-reduction approaches may also be relevant, including reuse of communication RS and, where applicable, use of data-bearing communication signals/channels for sensing. Data-bearing signals can be considered an overhead-reduction mechanism because they may reduce or avoid additional dedicated sensing RS resources. However, they should be studied with clear assumptions, since their sensing applicability depends on receiver knowledge of the transmitted data signal, data randomness, communication performance impact, and applicable sensing mode/scenario. Xiaomi | [Yes] | Support for the time-domain, cross-correlation: For sensing operation, cross-slot and cross-frame joint processing should typically be adopted, at least for Doppler or velocity estimation. RS sequences are periodically repeated per-frame in conventional communication systems. Such periodic repetition deteriorates the correlation properties of the sensing RS. Consequently, multiple spurious peaks emerge in the delay-Doppler correlation spectrum, which severely raises the probability of false alarm and drastically degrades target detection reliability. So, we think RS sequence randomization in time domain is studied for 6G ISAC to enhance the cross-correlation performance. For the range ambiguity, we have a question for our understanding: Range ambiguity is determined by the frequency-domain pattern of sensing reference signals. Could the FL/proponents kindly elaborate on how time-domain randomization of RS sequences impacts range ambiguity?
OPPO | Generally Yes | We think time-domain cross-correlation and range ambiguity are two different things. Could FL or the proponents help to explain the relation between time-domain randomization and range ambiguity?

For the last comment, if range ambiguity is problematic as it is also related to freq. comb pattern issue, we can remove it. Bracket is taken for the time being.
NTT DOCOMO |  | We are open to study these enhancements.
IDCC |  | We would like to include time/frequency processing as a method, i.e., [H] Proposal 4.1.5-3 For CP-OFDM enhancements to cross-correlation property, at least the following methods are studied for 6G ISAC. RS sequence randomization in time domain RS sequence spanning across multiple symbols Time-domain and/or frequency-domain processing (e.g., FDSS) of sensing signals/resources FFS: details of the definition of cross-correlation Other methods are not precluded.

Other waveforms

Background:

Regarding DFT-s-OFDM, the criteria for decision on whether DFT-s-OFDM is categorized as CP-OFDM enhancement or not is not that simple. However, from Moderator point of view, the following aspects were considered for this purpose.

Whether OFDM modulation blocks specified in 3GPP spec was kept unchanged. That is, cyclic prefix insertion after IFFT operation shall be kept unchanged.

In 6GR communication waveform agenda, only CP-OFDM was supported as a basis for 6GR DL communication waveform. That means, DFT-s-OFDM is considered as a separate waveform than CP-OFDM, even though the criteria 1) above is satisfied.

Moderator fully understands the ambiguity and difficulty in this kind of decision since e.g. DFT-s-OFDM can also be interpreted as CP-OFDM waveform from the criteria 1). However, at this point of discussion, DFT-s-OFDM is considered as other waveform than CP-OFDM.

There are contributions regarding other waveforms except CP-OFDM.

DFT-s-OFDM – Nokia, Spreadtrum, NEC, Huawei, HiSilicon, Offino, AT&T, FirstNet, Google, Tiami

Not support: Xiaomi, OPPO, Samsung

Pulse based on DFT-s-OFDM – Nokia, Xiaomi, CMCC, IDCC, ZTE, SJTU, Tiami, NTT DOCOMO, Google, Shanghai Jiao Tong University, NERCDTV

Pulse waveform not based on CP-OFDM –Lekha Wireless, China Unicom

LFM/FMCW/Chirp not based on CP-OFDM - Lekha Wireless, Transsion, IIT Kanpur

Phase continuity across symbols – vivo (smaller SCS only for guard band subcarriers)

OTFS - Lekha Wireless, NEC, Cohere Tech

AFDM - Lekha Wireless, ETRI, Shanghai Jiao Tong University, NERCDTV

pure Zak-OTFS overlay – Cohere Tech

Time gap – MediaTek

Chirp Periodic Prefix(CPP) and joint time-domain precoding – Pengcheng Laboratory

OCDM based on DFT-s-OFDM with frequency domain spreading – DOCOMO

OOK – Google

OSDM – University of Sheffield

No new waveform – Offino

Based on the contributions, 9 companies support DFT-s-OFDM as 6G ISAC waveform, and 3 companies do not support DFT-s-OFDM as CP-OFDM is fully sufficient. The main argument from 3 companies is that DFT-s-OFDM is only used for data and DMRS transmission in 5G NR, and that the low PAPR as the main advantage of DFT-s-OFDM over CP-OFDM is only relevant to data transmission, but not relevant to RS sequence transmission. Considering the number of supporting companies, the following FL proposal was made to collect more views on this issue.

[H] Proposal 4.2.1-2

In addition to CP-OFDM, DFT-s-OFDM waveform as defined for 6GR is the starting point for 6G ISAC UE transmission waveform study.

Study on enhancements on DFT-s-OFDM or other waveforms are not precluded.

Not support – vivo, IDCC, Samsung, Xiaomi, OPPO, Ericsson, Cohere

Waveforms up to implementation

Background:

There are discussions whether some sensing mode waveforms can be determined solely based on implementation. The suggested sensing modes are TRP-TRP bistatic, TRP-monostatic, and UE-monostatic sensing. There are contributions on this issues.

TRP-TRP bistatic sensing signal waveform is up to implementation

Support – Cohere Tech, Lenovo, Ericsson (at least for Rel-21)

Not support – Leka Wireless, CATT, CICTCI, Xiaomi, Interdigital, Panasonic, China Telecom, Qualcomm, DOCOMO (OFDM-compatible and unified for TRP/UE monostatic and TRP-TRP bistatic), LGE, IIT Kanpur, SONY

TRP monostatic sensing signal waveform is up to implementation

Support – Cohere Tech, Samsung, Lenovo, Ericsson (at least for Rel-21)

Not support – Leka Wireless, CATT, CICTCI, Xiaomi, Interdigital, Panasonic, Qualcomm, DOCOMO, LGE, IIT Kanpur SONY

UE monostatic sensing signal waveform is up to implementation

Support – Cohere Tech, Lenovo

Not support – Spreadtrum, CATT, CICTCI, Xiaomi, Interdigital, Panasonic, DOCOMO, LGE, IIT Kanpur, SONY

The majority of company views were that those sensing modes signals cannot be fully up to implementation, considering:

Regulation issue

Inter-vendor operability

Usage of a sensing signal to other sensing modes in addition to the intended sensing mode

Based on the contributions, following FL proposals were made for further discussions. If there are no consensus, it means that RAN1 concludes at least there are cases where TRP-TRP bistatic, TRP-monostatic, and UE-monostatic sensing signal waveform need to be specified.

[H] Proposal 4.3.1-2

There are cases where the specified TRP-TRP bistatic sensing signal waveform provides at least the following benfits:

Multi-vendor interoperability

Multi-static sensing reuse & Overhead reduction

Consistent signaling/procedures

Multi-TRP cooperation and fusion gains

Interference management

Consistent architecture and responsibility split

Aligned resource management

Predictable deployment behavior for operators

Consistency with positioning/sensing integration framework

[TABLE]
Company | Yes or No | Comments
Tiami | No | 
ZTE | No | It seems the proposal is opposite to the majority’s view. Also, the motivation of discuss the sensing RS/waveform per sensing mode is not clear. For sensing, our first priority is to have a unified design for all sensing modes. Even some sensing modes may not be specified in WI, it is still very beneficial to have a unified design. Different sensing modes can share the sensing RS and multi-static sensing can be efficiently supported. At least from 5G-A experience, the overhead of mono-static sensing cannot be neglected, and it will be disastrous if every sensing mode has a separate overhead. Based on the above, we have the following proposal: Avoid discussion of waveform/RS per sensing mode, and strive to design a unified RS/waveform scheme for all sensing modes, i.e. the sensing RS may be shared for multi-static sensing modes.
CATT, CICTCI | No | We align with ZTE. The design of waveforms and RS should be unified across all sensing modes. While some specific modes may not be fully addressed and will be left to implementation, it is essential to provide a consistent framework. From this perspective, a unified waveform/RS design is beneficial for implementation flexibility. Furthermore, a well-defined scope is crucial for inter-node interference identification and coordination, as well as multi-vendor interoperability. This also provides a mandatory performance baseline for multistatic sensing and RAN4 requirements.
vivo | Yes | 
SONY | No | 
Huawei, HiSilicon | Yes | TRP-TRP bi-static is of course up to implementation for single vendor operation. We disagree with the comment that we should go straight to have a unified design. Unifying design is not the starting point. What we should study first is what’s needed and beneficial for what scenario or purpose.
QC | No | Why TRP-TRP waveform and TRP-monostatic waveform should be specified: Prevents interoperability fragmentation across vendors (different sensing behaviors, coordination, reporting) Avoids inconsistent signaling/procedures (Tx/Rx coordination, triggering, control differ for mono vs bistatic) Enables Multistatic Sensing Reuse & Overhead Reduction (RS is being reused) Enables multi-TRP cooperation and fusion gains (needs common assumptions across nodes) Enables Interference Management (e.g. interference reduction at UEs, or at other TRPs) Ensures consistent architecture and responsibility split (SenF vs RAN vs TRP roles depend on sensing mode) Requires aligned resource management (monostatic local vs bistatic cross-node coordination cannot diverge) Provides predictable deployment behavior for operators (signaling load, coordination, scalability) Maintains consistency with positioning/sensing integration frameworks (timing, synchronization, reporting) Captures critical hardware/synchronization constraints explicitly

Specification benefits should be studied before concluding implementation-only.
Nokia |  | We are neutral on this
Samsung | Yes | Among those 6 sensing modes defined in 3GPP, only when both base station and UE are involved, the specification support of a standardized waveform shall be necessary, otherwise it seems no need to specify the exact waveform for other sensing modes for which the sensing waveform could be up to implementation with much less constraints.
NEC | NO | We think's it's not good for the inter vendor case.
CMCC | No | As we mentioned in our contribution, we support a unified design for all six sensing modes. Standardize waveform/RS for TRP-bistatic mode is beneficial for potential resource sharing among different sensing modes; and it is also beneficial for interference management. A TRP-bistatic RS which influence the TRP-UE DL receivers can be reassigned as a sensing RS.
MediaTek | YES | 
Xiaomi | No | For bistatic sensing, the transmitter and receiver are separate nodes, which may come from different vendors. It is therefore necessary to clearly specify the waveform used for the sensing reference signal (RS), because the receiver-side processing procedures and algorithms differ significantly across different waveforms.
OPPO | Slightly No | As an example, RIM-RS is specified in 5G for coordination between gNB’s. On the other hand, we think the proponents may need to firstly clarify whether TRP-TRP bi-static is limited to TRP’s of the same aNB or can be across different aNB’s. If TRP’s in a TRP-TRP bistatic sensing is limited to within one aNB, the proposal makes sense. If TRP’s in a TRP-TRP bistatic sensing can belong to different aNB and meanwhile the RS in intended to be measurable by UE as well, this touches another important discussion point in agenda 10.8.2: whether the DL sensing RS should be designed as intra-cell RS (like 5G CSI-RS) or cell-independent RS (like 5G PRS). We do not agree with ZTE’s view at this point that the RS should be sensing-mode transparent. It is too early to make such assessment.
Ericsson | YES | We are open to discussing the necessity for specifying it. But it is not clear to us why this is needed for 6G Day 1 sensing. While cross-vendor TRP-TRP bistatic sensing could motivate waveform standardization, the use case is limited (e.g., inter-network boundary scenarios) and is not considered necessary for 6G Day 1. The performance potential of a cross-vendor TRP-TRP solution is also limited by what kind of waveform options and information exchange has been standardized. Even if TRP-TRP bistatic is specified for the cross/vendor case, the key challenge for standardization is coordination (time/frequency synchronization, frame/resource alignment, and exchange of configuration/measurements), and specifically for the inter-aNB case which is upto RAN2&RAN3 and no RAN1 specification impact is needed.
LGE |  | Based on feedbacks and following the majority views, FL proposal was updated as Proposal 4.3.1-2. Let’s see whether the updated proposal is agreeable.
Panasonic |  | From regulation perspective, it is beneficial to study the necessity and potential benefits of specifying a waveform for each sensing mode. We support the direction of updated proposal.
Cohere | No | 
Huawei, HiSilicon | Disagree with update | For UE vendors who cared so much about TRP-TRP bi-static, please justify first the benefits on top of TRP monostatic and prove to us what issues for TRP-TRP the network vendors could not handle properly. Forget about the multi-vendor interoperability, before talking about interoperability, please prove there is such case TRP-TRP is more preferable for real deployment. We fully agree with Ericsson’s assessment as well on the key challenge of coordination (time/frequency synchronization, frame/resource alignment, and exchange of configuration/measurements), which is not just specification work but also pragmatic feasibility.
LGE | Yes | We support the revised proposal
Ericsson | NO, disagree with the proposed benefits | We echo Huawei’s views. Furthermore, we would like to clarify the following for each bullet points listed below, First of all, most of the listed points are not waveform issues at all! They are coordination, synchronization, signaling, architecture, and resource-management issues. Standardizing a waveform does not solve those problems magically. Interoperability is driven by synchronization accuracy, timing alignment, configuration exchange, and coordination procedures, none of which are RAN1 domain. Multi-static sensing reuse: This argument assumes the conclusion before the study has even started. It assumes that multistatic reuse is needed, that the same waveform should be reused across modes, but WE need to first clarify why such reuse is beneficial enough to justify standardization. overhead reduction: Let us do a pen-paper calculation. The TRP receiver has significantly better capabilities than a UE (e.g., larger antenna arrays, lower noise figure, and tighter synchronization). As a result, when reusing a TRP-only sensing signal for TRP-UE sensing, achieving comparable performance would likely require a substantially longer CPI. Let this difference be captured by a scaling factor , reflecting the gap in antenna gain, noise figure, and synchronization. In practice, can easily be on the order of 10 or more. Under reuse, the TRP-UE sensing function would then require approximately times more resources using the same waveform. Without reuse, the total resource usage would be (i.e., 1× for TRP-only sensing and × for TRP-UE sensing), meaning that reuse provides only a marginal overhead reduction of roughly , e.g., about 10% for Furthermore, is likely optimistic, and reuse may not always be feasible in practice (e.g., due to beamforming in different spatial directions as mentioned previously). Therefore, the actual overhead gain from reuse is expected to be significantly smaller than 10%. Consistent signaling/procedures: Procedures can be standardized even if waveform details remain implementation-specific. Again not RAN1 domain. Multi-TRP cooperation and fusion gains: Fusion gains rely more on synchronization and data exchange than on a mandated waveform. Interference management: Interference can be addressed through resource coordination, scheduling, and beam nulling etc., not only waveform specification. This was done for CLI in SBFD Rel-19. Consistent architecture and responsibility split: Functional split can be defined independently of whether the waveform is standardized. Again not RAN1 domain. Aligned resource management: Resource alignment does not require fixing the exact sensing waveform. Predictable deployment behavior for operators: Operators mainly need predictable procedures and coexistence behavior, not necessarily a fully specified waveform. Consistency with positioning/sensing integration framework: Not sure why we need this as there is no mandate to use/reuse the positioning framework.
NTT DOCOMO | No | TRP-TRP bi-static sensing waveform with standardization, enabling precise interference measurement and coordination. For interference management, it is better to deal with a known interference than an unknown one. A different sensing waveform for TRP-TRP bi-static sensing may also affect the frame structure, which has a specification impact on the UE side.

ZTE | No | It seems the proposal is opposite to the majority’s view. In 3GPP, we are discussing licensed spectrum, all design should comply with regulation. Without any specification, that means UE mono-static sensing mode is not supported. Without specification, interference management is impossible. Also, without specification, sensing RS from UE mono-static cannot be shared for UE bi-static which causes extra RS overhead. This is similar as TRP mono-static. Still, the motivation of discuss the sensing RS/waveform per sensing mode is not clear. For sensing, our first priority is to have a unified design for all sensing modes. Even some sensing modes may not be specified in WI, it is still very beneficial to have a unified design. Different sensing modes can share the sensing RS and multi-static sensing can be efficiently supported. At least from 5G-A experience, the overhead of mono-static sensing cannot be neglected, and it will be disastrous if every sensing mode has a separate overhead. Based on the above, we have the following proposal: Avoid discussion of waveform/RS per sensing mode, and strive to design a unified RS/waveform scheme for all sensing modes, i.e. the sensing RS may be shared for multi-static sensing modes.

Background:

There are discussions whether the 6GR communication data signals/channels can be used for sensing. There are contributions on this issue.

Study data for sensing

Support – Cohere Tech, Huawei, HiSilicon (CP-OFDM with pruning QAM, DFT-s-OFDM with floor clipping), China Telcom(opportunistic sensing), Southeast University, Sony

Not support – Xiaomi, Samsung (up to implementation), ZTE

The pros of using data for sensing is zero overhead. The cons of using data for sensing is the poor sensing performance and latency, tight dependency of sensing signal transmission to data transmission, non-guaranteed target sensing area. FL proposal was made based on the majority of company views.

[H] Proposal 4.3.4

Use of 6GR communication data signals/channels for sensing is studied for 6G ISAC.

Frame structure discussions

Background:

There are contributions on multiplexing between sensing and communication resources, which will not be discussed in agenda 10.8.3 but discussed in agenda 10.8.2 and. Here we focus on discussion about enhancement on CP length and SCS for 6G ISAC.

CP enhancement for ISAC

If a sensing target is located near the edge of the communication coverage, the sensing signal reflected by the sensing target can be received beyond the communication CP length by the sensing Rx. Following companies showed interest in studying the detection of the sensing target range beyond the communication CP length. Please note that one company argued that the advanced OFDM demodulation scheme based on multiple OFDM symbols would resolve the issue of delay exceeding CP length.

CP enhancement – Spreadtrum (ext. CP) , Lekha Wireless(adaptive CP), NEC, CATT, CICTCI, Xiaomi (CP extension, RIM-RS like CP), CMCC (freq. comb, 2OS-CP), Transsion, Interdigital, OPPO (freq. comb, 2OS-CP), Lenovo (freq. comb), China Telcom, NIST, ZTE(freq. comb, Multiple-OS-CP), AT&T, FirstNet(2 sequential RE merging), China Unicom, DOCOMO, LGE, ITRI, Acer Incorporated, Hanbat National University, Google, IIT Kanpur, vivo (phase continuity)

Not support – Qualcomm (Rx processing, multiple consecutive symbols Tx)

The handling of this issue is related to the effective CP length extension for sensing. One approach is to directly extend CP length for ISAC to cover the range beyond comm. CP length. The other approach is to achieve the same effect of the extended CP length instead of adjusting CP length for ISAC. Based on this observation, the following FL proposal was made for further discusssions.

[FL2][H] Proposal 5.1.1-2

For handling of a sensing signal reception beyond the communication CP length, if identified, at least the following methods are studied for 6G ISAC.

CP length extension by numerology and the impact on the number of symbols per slot

Effective CP length extension based on successive N OFDM symbols

Effective CP length extension based on frequency-domain comb pattern

Time gap before/after/within sensing signal

Effective CP length extension based on phase continuity across successive symbols

Transmission of RS in successive N OFDM symbols without CP length extension

RS sequence enhancement across symbols

By implementation withtout any spec impact

FFS: applicable sensing modes

FFS: whether applicable to dedicated sensing RS or RS shared with communication

FFS: impact on integration with communication

Other methods are not precluded.

Note: RAN1 strives for a solution that has maximum commonality with 6GR communication frame structure and numerology.

[TABLE]
Company | Yes or No | Comments
ZTE | Yes | The last bullet seems to be the same as the second one. If the last one is from ZTE’s proposal, we can remove it as it is duplicated. Also, could FL kindly make a clarification for the third bullet?

Huawei, HiSilicon | Comment | We believe the first step is to identify in which scenarios the sensing target range may exceed the CP length of communication. The second step is identifying the necessity of handling it by non-implementation methods.
QC | See comment | First, while we welcome a discussion on how to design for large sensing delays, it is important to recognize that sensing cannot be designed in isolation from communications. In particular, sensing cannot be assumed to operate under a numerology different from that of communications. Supporting multiple numerologies for a given band has historically proven to impose an undue burden on implementation teams and should therefore be avoided. Consequently, we suggest removing "CP length extension by numerology" from the list of candidate solutions. If this is not acceptable to the group, we request that a separate, dedicated discussion be triggered on whether a distinct numerology for ISAC is required. Suggestion: Remove "CP length extension by numerology" In addition, we propose to agree on the scenarios for which such issues may potentially arise. In our view, there is motivation to discuss special CP handling only for the TRP monostatic and TRP-TRP bistatic cases, as these are the configurations where sensing reflections with delays exceeding those encountered in typical communication deployments may occur. Suggestion: Add for which sensing modes this discussion is taking place. We propose: TRP monostatic and TRP-TRP bistatic. Furthermore, we assume that any resulting specification changes from this study — should specification impact be deemed necessary — would apply exclusively to dedicated sensing RS. Communication RS, even when reused for sensing purposes, should remain unaffected. Suggestion: Limit the discussion to dedicated sensing RS and not communication RS reuse. Beyond the above, we would like to highlight two additional methods that could address this issue: Method 1: Multi-symbol transmission with no specification impact. One approach is to transmit multiple consecutive OFDM symbols for sensing, without any additional specification changes, and rely on the receiver to perform multi-symbol FFT-based processing. This approach is transparent to the specification and imposes no additional standardization burden, therefore we would like to add the following bullet: Proposal: Add the following solution: Transmission of N successive OFDM symbols with no additional specification impact (e.g., at the Rx: multi-symbol FFT-based processing) Method 2: To address scenarios where target is within reasonable range, but the background clutter is seen with large delays, consider tx sequence enhancements to ensure constant ICI/ISI across sensing symbols. CP duration remains unchanged, but we ensure constant ICI/ISI across sensing symbols. The key insight is that, due to sensing delays associated with background clutter exceeding the CP length, ICI/ISI is introduced — and this interference varies across symbols. However, if the ICI/ISI profile is kept constant across sensing symbols, it manifests as a Doppler-0 component, and therefore does not significantly degrade sensing performance. A straightforward way to achieve this is to transmit the same sequence across consecutive sensing symbols, therefore we would like to add the following bullet: Proposal: Add the following solution: Across-symbol Tx sequence enhancements to mitigate the effects of delays exceeding the CP length"
IDCC | Comment | We support studying methods for handling sensing signal reception beyond the communication CP length. The study should be framed as extended effective guard time for sensing, not only CP extension. Candidate mechanisms include extended CP for sensing-related OFDM symbols, reduced number of OFDM symbols per slot to allow additional CP/guard time, guard periods before/after sensing RS symbols, muted-symbol-based guard mechanisms, and other equivalent methods.

SCS enhancement for ISAC

SCS define for 6GR communication may not be optimal/suitable for 6G ISAC. There are contributions that show interest in defining SCS for 6G ISAC for various reasons. Please note that one company does not support sensing-specific SCS because multi-symbol receiver processing and/or OFDM-based pulse-type waveform generation can resolve the claimed issues, and adding more SCS for sensing may introduce RF and coexistence challenges.

SCS enhancement – Spreadtrum (large/small SCS), vivo (only for guard band) , Lekha Wireless(adaptive SCS), Sharp, CATT, CICTCI, Transsion, Interdigital, China Telcom, China Unicom, LGE, ITRI, Acer Incorporated, Hanbat National University, CEWiT (lower SCS 7.5kHz), Google, IIT Kanpur (multiple SCS)

Not support – Qualcomm

According to the contributions, SCS larger than the communication SCS can provide the benefits including:

range resolution improvement

larger max. unambiguous Doppler estimation

robustness against phase noise

generation of CP-OFDM based pulse-type signal

SCS smaller than the communication SCS can provide the benefits including:

better Doppler estimation resolution

larger max. unambiguous range estimation

achieving phase continuity across symbols

better energy efficiency

Based on the contribution, the following FL proposal was made for further discussions.

[H] Proposal 5.1.2

At least the sensing-specific SCS is studied for 6G ISAC.

Sensing SCS smaller than 6GR communication SCS

Sensing SCS larger than 6GR communication SCS

FFS: impact on communication and implementation complexity.

Other enhancements are not precluded.

Evaluation of waveform and frame structure

Waveform characteristics

Background:

Regarding the evaluation methodology for waveform and frame structure, majority of companies supported to analyze theoretical waveform characteristics first, then perform either LLS or SLS to get more practical performance evaluations.

The company views on the metrics for the waveform characteristics are listed below.

Waveform characteristics analysis – Nokia, Spreadtrum, Lekha Wireless, Apple, Cohere Tech, CATT, CICTCI, Xiaomi, CMCC, Panasonic, NIST, ZTE, Qualcomm, DOCOMO, LGE, Ericsson, Tiami

Sensing net gain (Tx power gain-SNR degradation) - ZTE

Ambiguity Function/Auto-correlation – Nokia, Spreadtrum, CATT, CICTCI, Xiaomi, Transsion, Interdigital, OPPO, Samsung, NIST, ETRI, Qualcomm, DOCOMO, LGE, Ericsson, CEWiT, IIT Kanpur, Tiami

PSLR – Nokia, Spreadtrum, CATT, CICTCI, Xiaomi, Interdigital, ETRI, Qualcomm, COCOMO, Ericsson, IIT Kanpur, Tiami

ISLR – Nokia, CATT, CICTCI, Interdigital, NIST, ETRI, Qualcomm, DOCOMO, Ericsson

Resilience to ISI/ICI – Transsion, ETRI, Qualcomm, Ericsson (Doppler=0, non-zero) , IIT Kanpur, PCL

Multiplexing capability - ETRI

Indication of windowing assumptions - Ericsson

Based on the contributsions, the following FL proposal was made for further discussions.

[FL2][H] Proposal 6.1.1-3

For waveform/RS sequence evaluation for 6G ISAC, at least the following waveform/RS sequence characteristics are considered as the evaluation metrics.

Tx power efficiency

Link level simulation

Background:

Besides the waveform characteristics analysis, many companies supported running LLS or SLS to confirm the practical performance of the waveform and/or frame structure. From Moderator point of view, SLS will anyway be performed to check feasibility of 6G ISAC under agenda 10,.8.1. With this understanding, Moderator suggests to focus our discussion on whether LLS is required or not, in addition to the theoretical waveform characteristics. The details of LLS channel modeling will not be covered by this agenda, but by agenda 10.8.1.

The following contributions were observed regarding the necessity of LLS.

LLS – Nokia, OPPO, Lekha Wireless, Apple, Xiaomi, Samsung (incl. Rx side AF analysis), Lenovo, NIST, ZTE, LGE Pengcheng Laboratory, CEWiT

Based on existing CDL channel model, - OPPO

Add one or more clusters representing target(s) – Nokia, Xiaomi, Samsung, NIST

Update the parameters of one or more cluster to represent target(s) - Nokia, LGE (2nd priority)

Separate CDL channels for Tx-target link and target-Rx link, and concatenation; another CDL channel for background channel. – LGE (1st priority)

Reducing SLS model to single Tx and single Rx – Xiaomi, Sony, Qualcomm (single cell, interference-free, one/two ST, LOS STx-ST/ST-SRx, high/low SNR regimes)

According to the contributions, the necessity and benefits of running LLS for waveform/frame structure evaluation include:

Waveform characteristics analysis alone does not provide sufficient evidence in relation to the practical performance.

SLS performance is impacted not only by waveform performance itself, but also by other factors such as sensing entity dropping and background scatters.

LLS is the conventional method to evaluate waveform performance, which is simpler than SLS and more related to the final system performance than waveform characteristics analysis.

With these observations, the following FL proposal was made for further discussion.

with and without TX RX windowing, RS sequences and new waveforms other than CP-OFDM

vivo | No | AF should be defined with circular auto-correlation centralized by a Doppler shift, . This is because, in OFDM system, with a linear auto-correlation, CP introduced in OFDM system becomes meaningless. In addition, we provide the details to prove that with a circular auto-correlation, AF is just a 2D-DFT. If we prefer a discrete-time symbol of length (useful) plus CP of length with sampling period one OFDM symbol is for where negative indices are the CP (circular extension). A discrete ambiguity function (delay , Doppler index ) is for with some Doppler FFT length . This is exactly the same structure: circularity in due to CP, and a 2D correlation in delay–Doppler. For replacing with , we plug into and simplify it (using orthogonality of complex exponentials). The result is Let the time-domain sample of symbol be: for Global time index: . This is the standard OFDM ISAC transmit signal. The discrete AF of the whole OFDM ISAC waveform is: This is the true radar AF or canonical OFDM-ISAC AF, with and . Ignore the intra-symbol frequency shift (small Doppler, with no ICI), we can even approximate and just do a plain 2D FFT of to get a delay–Doppler map.
Huawei, HiSilicon | Yes | 
IDCC | Yes | 
Nokia | yes | We are fine with the proposal
ETRI | Yes | 
CMCC | Yes | We support to adopt this definition. Doppler dimension is necessary for waveform evaluation. A waveform/RS with best performance in delay measurement may not in practical due to its sensitivity to Doppler shift. For example, a thumbtack-shape ambiguity function is optimal in theory for delay-Doppler estimation, but requires a group of filter bank to deal with the Doppler shift, which significantly increase the complexity of the hardware/processing. The two-dimensional shape of the AF matters.
OPPO | Comments | Note that in Proposal 6.1.1, we have an FFS about linear AF or circular AF. Since linear AF or circular AF may impact the formula, we suggest to discuss this proposal after an agreement is achieved for Proposal 6.1.1.

NTT DOCOMO |  | There are two types of AF definitions, as described in Proposal 6.1.1. One is Circular-correlation-based AF (or periodic AF) and the other is Linear-correlation-based AF(or aperiodic AF), which AF definition to be used should be clarified first.
Moderator |  | Based on feedbacks and contributions, the proposal was updated as Proposal 7.1-2. Please continue discussions.
NTT DOCOMO | Comment | Linear or aperiodic AF should be used for AF definition. Based on the researches in radar systems, circular or periodic AF is typically used for continuous signals, and linear or aperiodic AF should be used for pulse signals. For 6G ISAC, even when the waveform is continuous (e.g., CP-OFDM), the sensing signals (including RS sequences) are transmitted in partial time resources in one CPI. If we treat the sensing signals across all the OFDM symbols in one CPI as a whole, it can be found that the sensing signals are not continuous but also kind of pulse signals, i.e., transmitted in non-contiguous OFDM symbols. In this case, linear or aperiodic AF should be the metric of sensing signal design. Furthermore, if pulse-type waveform is generated in CP-OFDM (or DFT-s-OFDM), the linear or aperiodic AF should also be considered. Therefore, for a unified metric for any sensing waveform, linear or aperiodic AF should be defined. For example, the linear (or aperiodic) AF at normalized doppler v could be defined as:

Parameters | Values

vivo

Proposal 1: RAN1 studies a unified, symbol level ISAC waveform in consideration of symbol-phase continuity that remains compatible with OFDM while enabling high resolution sensing, efficient resource sharing, and minimal interference.

Proposal 7: RAN1 concludes that the pulse shaping filter does not affect the reuse of the guard band as sensing resources if phase continuity across consecutive OFDM symbols is maintained. Under this condition, the pulse shaping operation preserves smooth symbol transitions and does not introduce additional constraints on guard band utilization.

Proposal 8: In the utilization of guard bands for sensing, two alternatives of configuring BWP for sensing can be accounted for as follows:

Alt-1: Configure a BWP for sensing only, using both separated guard bands (either partial or full resources) in both frequency boundaries of carrier with an independent numerology compared to the numerology applied to the data stream. In this case, the UE is only allowed to receive sensing signal from the guard band-based BWP at a time.

Alt-2: Configure a BWP for both data and sensing, using RBs in transmission bandwidth as well as both separated guard bands (either partial or full resources) in both frequency boundaries of carrier with the numerology that is 1/M of the numerology applied to the data stream, where M is the number of consecutive OFDM symbols in guard bands dedicated for sensing.

Leka Wireless

Proposal 2: It is proposed to study waveform requirements across different sensing modes, including TRP monostatic, TRP–TRP bistatic, and UE monostatic. It is further proposed to investigate a unified waveform framework with mode-dependent configurations, including:

• Orthogonality for bistatic sensing

• Low-PAPR configurations for UE sensing

EURECOM

Proposal 3: PDCCH used to indicate sensing resource can be transmitted in the same or different CORSET as PDCCH used to indicate communication resource.

Proposal 8: In one mode, sensing resources are preconfigured to the UE by the aNB through DCI or RRC signaling. The period of the sensing resources is indicated by DCI or RRC signaling.

Proposal 9: In another mode, the UE requests the aNB to configure sensing resource through UCI when it needs to carry out sensing task then the aNB configures sensing resource through DCI.

Tejas Network

Proposal 1: Instead of resetting the TA-offset specifically for sounding symbols, the more effective approach is to adjust the measured delay afterward during post-processing, even if the delay exceeds the cyclic prefix.

Proposal 2: Comb Size 1 Maximizes Unambiguous Range.

Proposal 3: Repeating symbols not only enable partial correlation but also support beam sweeping and enhance angle-of-arrival (AoA) estimation.

NEC

Proposal 1: The sensing waveform should achieve balanced performance, low implementation complexity, and good forward compatibility with existing 3GPP communication.

Proposal 4: Study the CP length design of sensing symbols associated with the number of sensing symbols within a slot.

Sharp

Proposal 2: Sensing mode specific waveform is not considered for 6GR. RAN1 evaluates the necessity of mode-specific waveform (if any) using a common methodology:

• Step 1: Evaluate enhanced CP-OFDM under each sensing mode.

• Step 2: Identify any residual performance gap relative to the use-case requirement.

• Step 3: Justify mode-specific waveform specification only where the residual gap is material and cannot be closed by enhanced CP-OFDM or frame structure enhancement.

Proposal 4: New waveforms are not endorsed by RAN1 on the basis of theoretical analysis alone. LLS results, and where applicable SLS results, are required to support new-waveform proposals.

Apple

Proposal 3: RAN1 should study whether the sensing waveform and/or sensing transmission requirements within the transmission gap should be specified.

CATT, CICTCI

Proposal 6: For TRP-TRP bistatic sensing mode, further study:

- The need and details of frame structure alignment among TRPs, considering factors such as inter-vendor collaboration, TA adjustment, etc.

- The impact on UE, if any.

Proposal 14: RAN1 should study the potential benefits and specification impacts of standardizing the TRP monostatic sensing waveform, with the study scope including at least the following items:

• Providing a performance baseline for multistatic sensing and RAN4 testing;

• Avoiding ghost target issues;

• Supporting inter-node interference identification and coordination.

Proposal 15: RAN1 should study the necessity, potential benefits, and specification impacts of standardizing the TRP-TRP bistatic sensing waveform, with the study scope including at least the following items:

• Providing a performance baseline for multistatic sensing and RAN4 testing;

• Supporting multi-vendor interoperability.

Proposal 16: RAN1 should study the necessity of waveform enhancements for UE monostatic sensing as well as the corresponding specification impacts, with the study scope including at least the following items:

• Mechanism for UEs to acquire sensing resources;

• Power control for sensing-induced interference.

TCL

Proposal 3: RAN1 to study and clearly define the sensing symbol structure, considering at least the following two options:

• Option 1: Bi-directional sensing symbol, where a single symbol used for both transmitting the ISAC reference signal and monitoring the reflected echo.

• Option 2: Uni-directional sensing symbols, where separate symbols used for transmitting the ISAC reference signal and monitoring the reflected echo.

Interdigital

Proposal 1: RAN1 should study 6G ISAC-specific waveform and/or frame-structure enhancements relative to the agreed CP-OFDM waveform and 6GR communication frame-structure starting points. Further consideration of such enhancements should be limited to cases where the agreed starting points show limitations or gaps in meeting the relevant sensing requirements/KPIs or communication-integration requirements for the considered sensing mode, scenario, and operating assumptions.

Proposal 2: RAN1 should compare 6G ISAC waveform and frame-structure candidates using a common comparison basis, including at least:

• sensing mode and scenario;

• sensing signal/resource configuration;

• RE mapping and sensing resource ratio/overhead;

• observation interval/CPI;

• numerology, bandwidth, and transmit power/energy;

• receiver processing;

• channel and interference model;

• communication integration impact, including coexistence and multiplexing.

Proposal 7: For time-domain and/or frequency-domain processing of sensing signals/resources, RAN1 should study at least:

• where the processing is applied, e.g., transmitter side, receiver side, or both;

• whether the processing is applied to sensing RS/sequence generation, RE/resource mapping, OFDM-symbol-level samples, and/or receiver-side sensing processing;

• required receiver knowledge or configuration of the processing;

• impact on CP-OFDM compatibility, communication coexistence, and baseband implementation complexity.

Proposal 8: For pulse-type and FMCW/LFM-type sensing waveform/signal candidates, RAN1 should study how such candidates are introduced relative to the agreed CP-OFDM waveform starting point, including at least:

• realization within CP-OFDM-based signal/resource design;

• multiplexing with CP-OFDM communication or sensing resources;

• use of dedicated sensing resources where a dedicated waveform/signal structure is assumed.

Proposal 14: RAN1 should study sensing-resource time-domain organization over the 6GR communication frame structure, including at least:

• sensing occasion structure, including placement and duration of sensing resources;

• repetition pattern across symbols/slots/subframes/frames for coherent or non-coherent processing;

• CPI / observation interval formation over one or more sensing occasions for delay/Doppler estimation.

Proposal 15: RAN1 should study frequency-domain comb-size and resource-mapping aspects for sensing RS/resources, including at least:

• sensing RS comb size, including comb size different from communication RS where applicable;

• sensing bandwidth occupation, including contiguous or distributed frequency-domain allocation;

• frequency-domain mapping of sensing resources relative to the 6GR communication resource grid.

Samsung

Proposal 1 RAN1 discuss the sensing-oriented requirements that waveform and frame structure should support, as the basis for guiding candidate design directions and their trade-offs.

Proposal 16 RAN1 assume a common OFDM-based receiver front-end.

Panasonic

Proposal 5: Study 6G ISAC waveform based on the following step:

Step 1. Study 6G ISAC waveform by reusing 6GR CP-OFDM for communication.

Step 2. If Step 1. does not satisfy the 6G ISAC requirement, then study 6G ISAC waveform by enhancement of 6GR CP-OFDM communication.

Step 3. If Step 2. does not satisfy the 6G ISAC requirement, then study new waveform for 6G ISAC.

Huawei/HiSilicon

Proposal 3: As one further step to move forward, the proponents can justify the relative gain of the enhancement compared to the benchmark using the channel model decided by the proponents for the waveform/sequence study for ISAC.

Proposal 7: NR reference signals (RS), e.g., CSI-RS, and SRS, can be the starting point for sensing RS design and evaluation for Type1 resource that is sensing performance oriented.

Proposal 11: NR reference signals (RS), such as CSI-RS, and SRS, can be the starting point for the RS design and evaluation for Type2 resource that is shared with communication.

China Telcom

Proposal 4: For monostatic sensing, study which operation mode (simultaneous Tx/Rx or non-simultaneous Tx/Rx) is suitable, since this affects waveform design, self-interference handling and frame-structure support.

ZTE

Proposal 2: 6GR sensing RS should be compatible with communication hardware.

Proposal 7: Avoid discussion of waveform/RS per sensing mode, and strive to design a unified RS/waveform scheme for all sensing modes, i.e. the sensing RS may be shared for multi-static sensing modes.

Proposal 11: Study the sensing net gain to evaluate the overall/final performance of sensing signal using the following formula.

Sensing Net Gain [dB] = TX power gain relative to the reference – SNR degradation relative to the reference

TX power gain is determined by the waveform analysis

SNR degradation is determined by

Option 1: Theoretical SNR degradation by waveform analysis

Option 2: Simulated SNR degradation by LLS/SLS

Pengcheng Laboratory

Proposal 1: It is proposed that ISAC waveform design for 6G high-mobility scenarios shall account ISI (Inter-Symbol Interference) and ICI (Inter-Carrier Interference) to ensure reliable communication and sensing performance.

Proposal 2: It is proposed to explore waveform design approaches that treat ISI (Inter-Symbol Interference) and ICI (Inter-Carrier Interference) not only as interference to be mitigated, but also as a source of information for sensing enhancement, leveraging the time-varying propagation characteristics inherent in high-mobility channels.

Proposal 4: Study the scalability of the enhanced CP-OFDM frame structure to MU-MIMO scenarios, including user-specific chirp parameter configuration and inter-layer interference suppression in the Delay-Doppler domain.

Proposal 5: We suggest that RAN1 considers supporting “[FL3][H] Proposal 4.2.2-5” in R1-2602984 as a framework for studying CP-OFDM waveform and RS sequence enhancements for 6G ISAC. We further suggest that all listed enhancement aspects be considered for study without presuming priority order. Companies are encouraged to identify which aspects are most relevant to their proposed solutions while noting that no enhancement aspect would be deprioritized or excluded without sufficient study justification.

Proposal 6: For evaluating "Resilience to ISI and/or ICI" under the above framework, we would like to propose the following methodology as a starting point for discussion:

Applicable scenarios: High-mobility scenarios with UE speed ≥ 300 km/h (e.g., HST, highway)

Applicable sensing modes: TRP monostatic (moving target), UE-TRP bistatic, TRP-UE bistatic

Key metrics:

For communication: BER floor under high Doppler (normalized Doppler shift ≥ 0.1)

For sensing: RMSE degradation of range/velocity estimation compared to low-mobility baseline

Baseline: CP-OFDM without any ISI (Inter-Symbol Interference) and/or ICI (Inter-Carrier Interference) mitigation enhancement

Recommended evaluation method: LLS with time-varying channel model (e.g., TDL-D or CDL-D with maximum Doppler corresponding to target UE speed)

ETRI

Proposal 1: Study a method for performing mono-static sensing on a connected UE in order to reduce the transmission timing error that most significantly affects sensing accuracy in bi-static/multi-static sensing modes, with particular focus on the following aspects:

Normal UE with mobility of 3km/h (lower priority for a fixed reference UE)

KPI at the TRP side: Precision level

KPI at the UE side: Power consumption level

Proposed 7: Study the following aspects of TDM-based dedicated sensing slot/symbol design for 6G ISAC frame structure:

Sensing slot duration and symbol structure within a slot

CPI structure and periodicity for Doppler estimation

Multi-TRP sensing slot orthogonalization via chirp rate or RS sequence assignment

RRC/MAC-CE signalling for sensing resource set configuration

Shanghai Jiao Tong University, NERCDTV

Proposal 5: RAN1 to investigate AFDM as a candidate waveform for 6G ISAC systems, evaluating its parameter optimization towards high-efficiency sensing, high-mobility robustness, low PAPR, and backward compatibility with OFDM-based architectures.

Proposal 6: RAN1 to study and specify the design of AFDM parameters (e.g., c_1 and c_2), low-complexity receiver algorithms for communication, sensing, and PAPR reduction, and their integration into a 6G-compatible system architecture, to enhance robustness against doubly-selective channels while targeting superior performance in sensing, high-mobility, and NTN scenarios.

Proposal 7: RAN1 to investigate the implications of AFDM on MIMO integrated pilot design, target angle estimation, and joint receiver signal processing, etc., and to study low-complexity sensing techniques to ensure the efficient integration of AFDM with existing multi-antenna ISAC systems.

Southeast university

Proposal 2: RAN1 should acknowledge and study the deterministic-random tradeoff inherent in sensing with data-bearing physical channels, including its impact on sensing stability, communication performance, and applicable deployment assumptions.

Proposal 3: RAN1 should study ESL, EISL, and EWISL as statistical metrics for sensing with data-bearing physical channels, including their use in evaluating pulse-shaping and constellation-statistics impacts on sensing performance.

PHY Wireless

Proposal 1: 3GPP should prioritize downlink multistatic TRP-to-UE sensing as an initial 6G ISAC configuration.

Sony

Proposal 3: Support the study of 6G ISAC waveforms in multi-node cooperative sensing scenarios. (e.g., whether the candidate 6G ISAC waveform can be better than CP-OFDM in cooperative sensing scenarios).

AT&T, FirstNet

Proposal 4: Beamforming may change depending on state of sensing in the network and should be able to be dynamically configured. Beamforming can be target-specific.

LGE

Proposal 21 If ISAC LLS channel modelling is agreed, ISAC LLS channel can be modelled with the baseline CDL-D model, with the following changes:

Define random or fixed target position with respect to the sensing TX and RX

Select the LOS AoA/AoD in accordance with target position, modify cluster angles in Table 7.7.1-4 accordingly

Generate normalized CIR for each antenna pair following Section 7.7.1 of [7]

If relevant, add propagation delay corresponding to the sensing TX-ST, ST-sensing RX distances.

Ericsson

Proposal 1: For 6G sensing study, RAN1 prioritizes TRP-UE and UE-TRP bistatic sensing modes. Once the basic framework for TRP-UE and UE-TRP mode is accomplished, RAN1 can consider the necessary changes for UE-UE bistatic and UE monostatic modes.

Proposal 2: Confirm CP-OFDM waveform as the baseline for 6G ISAC waveform.

Google

Proposal 9: Support configuring the UE to perform sensing operations periodically, semi-persistently, or aperiodically based on dynamic triggering or activating signals from the network

ANNEX: Agreements

RAN1#124-bis

Agreement:

CP-OFDM waveform as defined for 6GR is the starting point for 6G ISAC waveform study.

Study on enhancements on CP-OFDM or other waveforms is not precluded.

Agreement:

6GR communication frame structure is the starting point for 6G ISAC frame structure study, in at least the following aspects.

Frame/sub-frame/slot/symbol structure

CP length

SCS

Enhancements on frame structure/above aspects are not precluded.

Agreement:

Companies are encouraged to provide views on necessity/pros/cons/metrics of LLS and/or SLS and pros/cons/metrics of theoretical waveform characteristics analysis, for evaluation of ISAC waveform and/or integration with communication, to RAN1#125 meeting.

Agreement:

CP-OFDM is used as the benchmark for evaluating the benefits of sensing waveforms.

Dalian, May 18th ~ 22nd, 2026

Agenda item: 10.8.3

Source: Moderator (LG Electronics)

Title: Summary on Waveform and frame structure for 6G ISAC

Document for: Discussion/Decision

Work Plan for RAN1#126

We had good progress given very limited time allocation. Moderator really appreciates all delegates’ being quite constructive in discussions during the meeting.

Based on the agreements made in RAN1#125, the following topics will be prioritized for discussion in RAN1#126.

Study of the potential solutions for enhancement based on CP-OFDM for sensing RS, including the following aspects:

Relevant enhancement direction

Applicable sensing resources (dedicated and/or shared)

Applicable sensing modes

Study of the potential solutions for handling a sensing signal reception beyond the CP length of the communication OFDM symbol, including the following aspects:

Applicable sensing modes

Applicable sensing resources (dedicated and/or shared)

Impact on communication system/performance

Resource overhead consideration

Study of the detailed metrics for waveform/RS sequence characteristics analysis

PAPR

Tx power gain

Ambiguity function/auto-correlation

Cross-correlation

Out-of-band characteristics

Resilience to interference

Study of waveform/frame structure evaluation metrics in addition to waveform/RS sequence characteristics analysis

Sensing performance related metrics

Communication impact related metrics

Tx/Rx implementation related metrics

Standardization impact related metrics

Common evaluation assumptions/scenarios for comparison based on LLS and a simplified SLS

Introduction

In RAN #108, the SID on Study on 6G Radio was agreed, which includes the following objectives for 6G ISAC [1].

[TABLE]
Sensing – Studies to be based on use cases and associated requirements, as defined in [TR38.914] PHY functions and procedures for sensing technology (e.g., waveform. reference signals, measurement feedback, etc…) [RAN1, RAN4] Evaluate sensing performance and if necessary, extend channel modelling, for the selected use cases [RAN1] Aspects of integration with communication services [RAN1] higher layer procedures and protocol aspects [RAN2] RAN4 aspects of sensing including RF, coexistence, and testability in coordination with other WGs [RAN4] Note: RAN1 identify detailed requirements, if triggered by TSG RAN

This document summarizes the contributions and discussions on sub-agenda 10.8.3 Waveform and frame structure for ISAC.

[TABLE]
ISAC Note 1: Including PHY functionalities and procedures for ISAC Evaluations Note 1: Including deployment scenarios, performance evaluation methodologies/metrics/KPIs for the target use cases, and potential extension of channel model, if necessary, Aspects of integration with communication Note 1: Including proposals for reusing and dedicated reference signal based on waveforms for communications, measurement and report for different use cases, etc. (could be part of AI 10.5.3) Waveform and frame structure Note 1: Including proposals for potential enhancement based on communication waveform (e.g., low PAPR waveform enhancement, longer CP length, larger SCS etc.), potential new waveform, frame structure, and corresponding analysis on performance benefit and impact in terms of integration with communication.

This document follows the convention below for improving readability:

The proposals in this document are tagged with different color based on discussion priority:

[H] Proposal: Proposal to be discussed with High Priority.

[M] Proposal: Proposal to be discussed with Medium Priority.

[L] Proposal: Proposal to be discussed with Low Priority

The proposal version (the last digit of the proposal number) will increase if there is any update on the proposal from the previous round. If there is no update on the proposal from the previous round, there will be no increase on the proposal version.

This agenda will cover the following topics:

Waveform

CP-OFDM enhancement for 6G ISAC

Sensing RS sequence design

Other waveforms for 6G ISAC

Frame structure

CP enhancement for 6G ISAC

SCS enhancement for 6G ISAC

Evaluation of waveform/frame structure

Evaluation based on waveform characteristics analysis

Evaluation based on Link-Level Simulation

The following topics will be covered by agenda 10.8.2

Resource allocation & Multiplexing of sensing signal

Sensing RS pattern design

The following topics will be covered by agenda 10.8.1

LLS channel modeling for 6G ISAC

For more constructive discussions within very limited time schedule for 6G SI ISAC agenda, Moderator tried to make FL Proposals based on the contributions supported by majority of companies, rather than a single or a few companies.

Proposed online/offline proposals

Monday

Tuesday

[H] Proposal 4.1.1-4

At least the following enhancement directions for CP-OFDM are studied for 6G ISAC.

Enhancement to PAPR/Output Back-Off(OBO)/Tx power gain

Enhancement to [Ambiguity Function(AF)]/auto-correlation properties (PSLR/ISLR, main lobe width)

Enhancement to joint PAPR and AF properties

Resilience to interference

[Resilience to ACLR(Adjacent Channel Leakage Ratio)/OOBE(Out-Of-Band Emission)]

Enhancement to improve sensing resource utilization efficiency

Enhancement to sensing coverage

Enhancement to cross-correlation

Other enhancements are not precluded.

Any combination of multiple enhancements are not precluded.

[H] Proposal 4.1.2.1-2

For CP-OFDM enhancements to PAPR/Output Back-Off(OBO)/Tx power gain/Net gain, at least the following methods are studied for 6G ISAC.

Zadoff-Chu sequence enhancement (including LFM/FMCW/Chirp-type waveform generation)

Gold sequence enhancement

[Use of LFM sequence]

[Duty ratio optimization]

[Quasi-complementary sequence set (QCSS)]

Use of pi/2-BPSK

Other methods are not precluded.

[H] Proposal 4.1.2.2-2

For CP-OFDM enhancements to AF properties, at least the following methods are studied for 6G ISAC.

Zadoff-Chu sequence enhancement

Gold sequence enhancement

[Use of NLFM sequence]

[Non-transparent] FDSS(Frequency-Domain Spectrum Shaping)

Quasi-complementary sequence set (QCSS)

Other methods are not precluded.

[H] Proposal 4.1.3-3

For CP-OFDM enhancements to sensing coverage enhancement, at least the following pulse-type waveform generation methods at least for monostatic sensing are studied for 6G ISAC.

RS sequence-based generation at least in frequency domain

Frequency domain comb pattern and time masking-based generation

SCS-based generation

Other methods are not precluded.

[H] Proposal 4.2.2

At least pulse-type waveform generation based on DFT-s-OFDM is studied for 6G ISAC.

Other waveforms are not precluded.

[H] Proposal 6.2.1-3

[working assumption]

For waveform evaluation for 6G ISAC, a simplified SLS is performed in addition to theoretical waveform characteristics analysis.

Details of a simplified SLS is covered by agenda 10.8.1

The usage/necessity of simplified SLS is considered separately for different use cases.

LLS (6)

Simplified SLS (11) – single Tx/Rx, single target

Full SLS (1)

[FL2][H] Proposal 6.2.1-7 – offline consensus

Theoretical waveform/RS sequence characteristics analysis is done for waveform/RS sequence evaluation for 6G ISAC.

Companies [should/are encouraged to] provide either LLS or a simplified SLS in addition to the theoretical waveform/RS sequence. It’s up to company how to model LLS or a simplified SLS.

FFS: applicable evaluation cases

[FL2][H] Proposal 4.1 – off-offline consensus

For the of CP-OFDM, at least the following methods are considered.

Zadoff-Chu sequence enhancement

Gold sequence enhancement

LFM/Chirp-like sequence (incl. frequency sweeping rate/slope)

Quasi-complementary sequence set (QCSS)

Transparent/Non-transparent Tx time-domain processing and/or frequency-domain processing (e.g., FDSS)

Pi/2 BPSK

Non-Linear FM sequence

Phase continuity in the sensing resource block the guard band

[Zak-OTFS-over-CP-OFDM – superposition of Zak-OTFS to CP-OFDM subcarriers]

RS sequence randomization in time domain

RS sequence spanning across multiple symbols

FFS: whether applicable to dedicated resource and/or shared resource with communication
